=== Example 0 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if a worksheet is not dispensable. From premise 6, we know that a worksheet is either paper or is environment-friendly. If it is paper, then from premise 3, a worksheet is woodware, and from premise 2, a worksheet is dispensable. If it is environment-friendly, we know it is good from premise 5, but we know nothing about whether it is dispensable. Therefore, we don't know if a worksheet is dispensible or not, so the statement is uncertain.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona. From premise 1, we know that a La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another if it receives more points. From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate the statement "if Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel laureate". Let's assume that Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner. This doesn't tell us anything about whether Amy is a Nobel laureate, so the statement isn't true, meaning it is either False or Uncertain. To distinguish between the two, notice that we could have a scenario where Amy is neither an Olympic gold medal winner nor a Nobel laureate. None of the premises are violated in this case. This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
If a person pays their taxes, then they contribute to the country.
Everyone who works for a government department pays a tax on their salary.
Everyone in the army is an employee of a government department.
Everyone convicted of murder goes to prison.
Everyone who has been to prison has a criminal record.
James was either once convicted of murder, or spent time in prison.
James either has a criminal record, or pays his taxes.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
James does not contribute to the country.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if James contributes to the country. Let's think about what we know about James. First, we know that James was either sentenced for thief or stayed in prison. However, this doesn't tell us anything about whether James contributed to the country. Second, we know that James either had a bad record in the local state or that he was respected by others. However, the premises don't tell us anything about the relationship between having a bad record and contributing to the country. Therefore, it is uncertain whether James contributes to the country.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
No songs are visuals.
All folk songs are songs.
All videos are visuals.
All movies are videos.
All sci-fi movies are movies.
Inception is a sci-fi movie.
Mac is neither a folk song nor a sci-fi movie.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Inception is a folk song.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if Inception is a folk song. We know that Inception is a sci-fi movie. Since all movies are videos and Inception is a movie, it is a video, which means it is visual. On the other hand, we know that all folk songs are songs, and no songs are visual, so no folk songs are visual. Therefore, since Inception is visual but no folk songs are visual, we know that Inception cannot be a folk song, so the statement is false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Every chef can cook.
Some people who aren’t chefs can cook.
People who cook can make scrambled eggs and pasta.
If someone can make cookies and muffins, they are a baker.
Bakers who can also make scrambled eggs can make a good breakfast.
Luke can make cookies, scrambled eggs, and muffins, but not pasta.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Luke is a chef.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if Luke can make a good breakfast. From the last premise, we know that Luke can make cookies, scrambled eggs, and muffins. Since Luke can make cookies and muffins, they are a baker. Now, combining the information we have, since Luke is a baker and can make scrambled eggs, this means that they can make a good breakfast. Therefore, Luke can make a good breakfast, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
ETS develops various standardized tests primarily in the United States for K-12 and higher education.
ETS administers international tests, including the TOEFL, TOEIC, GRE, and subject tests.
Many of the assessments ETS develops are associated with entry to the US tertiary and quaternary education institutions.
ETS also develops K-12 statewide assessments used for accountability testing in many states.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
ETS doesn't administer tests internationally.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if ETS develops assessments for K-12 statewide as well as entry to US tertiary and quaternary educatiand doon institutions. We know that ETS develops assessments for K-12 statewide. We also know that ETS develops assessments associated with entry to the US tertiary and quaternary education institutes. Therefore, both parts of the conclusion are true, and the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Daveed Diggs is an actor and film producer.
Daveed Diggs played two roles in the musical Hamilton on Broadway.
One of the actors from Hamilton won the best actor award.
The actor playing Thomas Jefferson won the best actor award.
Daveed Diggs played Thomas Jefferson.
Musicals on Broadway are not films.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Daveed Diggs won the best actor award.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if there is a person from BRICS speaking Hindi. We know that there is an Indian, and since India is one of BRICS, we know that there is an Indian in BRICS. Furthermore, we know that they speak either Hindi or English, however, we don't know which one. Therefore, there could be a person in BRICS speaking Hindi, or there could not. Therefore, it is uncertain whether there is a person from BRICS speaking Hindi.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Miroslav Venhoda was a Czech pianist who specialized in the study of hieroglyphics, machine learning, and badminton.
Any pianist is a chef.
Some chefs enjoy music.
Miroslav Venhoda burned a book in 1946 called Method of Studying Gregorian Chant.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
No pianist specialized in machine learning.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if Miroslav Venhoda specialized in machine learning. From the premises, we know that Miroslav Venhoda was a pianist who specialized in the study of hieroglyphics, machine learning, and badminton. Therefore, since he is a pianist, we cannot conclude that no pianist specialized in machine learning. Therefore, the statement is false.
ANSWER: False
Processed: False

Reference: False

</PREMISES>

To distinguish between the two, notice that we could have a scenario where Amy is neither an Olympic gold medal winner nor a Nobel laureate. None of the premises are violated in this case. This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if a worksheet is not dispensable. From premise 6, we know that a worksheet is either paper or is environment-friendly. If it is paper, then from premise 3, a worksheet is woodware, and from premise 2, a worksheet is dispensable. If it is environment-friendly, we know it is good from premise 5, but we know nothing about whether it is dispensable. Therefore, we don't know if a worksheet is dispensible or not, so the statement is uncertain.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.

Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

Therefore, Luke can make a good breakfast, so the statement is true.

=== Example 7 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if a worksheet is not dispensable. From premise 6, we know that a worksheet is either paper or is environment-friendly. If it is paper, then from premise 3, a worksheet is woodware, and from premise 2, a worksheet is dispensable. If it is environment-friendly, we know it is good from premise 5, but we know nothing about whether it is dispensable. Therefore, we don't know if a worksheet is dispensible or not, so the statement is uncertain.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona. From premise 1, we know that a La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another if it receives more points. From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate the statement "if Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel laureate". Let's assume that Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner. This doesn't tell us anything about whether Amy is a Nobel laureate, so the statement isn't true, meaning it is either False or Uncertain. To distinguish between the two, notice that we could have a scenario where Amy is neither an Olympic gold medal winner nor a Nobel laureate. None of the premises are violated in this case. This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
If a person pays their taxes, then they contribute to the country.
Everyone who works for a government department pays a tax on their salary.
Everyone in the army is an employee of a government department.
Everyone convicted of murder goes to prison.
Everyone who has been to prison has a criminal record.
James was either once convicted of murder, or spent time in prison.
James either has a criminal record, or pays his taxes.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
James does not contribute to the country.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if James contributes to the country. Let's think about what we know about James. First, we know that James was either sentenced for thief or stayed in prison. However, this doesn't tell us anything about whether James contributed to the country. Second, we know that James either had a bad record in the local state or that he was respected by others. However, the premises don't tell us anything about the relationship between having a bad record and contributing to the country. Therefore, it is uncertain whether James contributes to the country.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
No songs are visuals.
All folk songs are songs.
All videos are visuals.
All movies are videos.
All sci-fi movies are movies.
Inception is a sci-fi movie.
Mac is neither a folk song nor a sci-fi movie.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Inception is a folk song.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if Inception is a folk song. We know that Inception is a sci-fi movie. Since all movies are videos and Inception is a movie, it is a video, which means it is visual. On the other hand, we know that all folk songs are songs, and no songs are visual, so no folk songs are visual. Therefore, since Inception is visual but no folk songs are visual, we know that Inception cannot be a folk song, so the statement is false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.

The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.


<PREMISES>

All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.

</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

If it is environment-friendly, we know it is good from premise 5, but we know nothing about whether it is dispensable. Therefore, we don't know if a worksheet is dispensible or not, so the statement is uncertain.

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona. From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.

This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

This means the statement must be false.

=== Example 14 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if a worksheet is not dispensable. From premise 6, we know that a worksheet is either paper or is environment-friendly. If it is paper, then from premise 3, a worksheet is woodware, and from premise 2, a worksheet is dispensable. If it is environment-friendly, we know it is good from premise 5, but we know nothing about whether it is dispensable. Therefore, we don't know if a worksheet is dispensible or not, so the statement is uncertain.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona. From premise 1, we know that a La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another if it receives more points. From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

Therefore, since Inception is visual but no folk songs are visual, we know that Inception cannot be a folk song, so the statement is false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

=== Example 17 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if a worksheet is not dispensable. From premise 6, we know that a worksheet is either paper or is environment-friendly. If it is paper, then from premise 3, a worksheet is woodware, and from premise 2, a worksheet is dispensable. If it is environment-friendly, we know it is good from premise 5, but we know nothing about whether it is dispensable. Therefore, we don't know if a worksheet is dispensible or not, so the statement is uncertain.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona. From premise 1, we know that a La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another if it receives more points. From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate the statement "if Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel laureate". Let's assume that Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner. This doesn't tell us anything about whether Amy is a Nobel laureate, so the statement isn't true, meaning it is either False or Uncertain. To distinguish between the two, notice that we could have a scenario where Amy is neither an Olympic gold medal winner nor a Nobel laureate. None of the premises are violated in this case. This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
If a person pays their taxes, then they contribute to the country.
Everyone who works for a government department pays a tax on their salary.
Everyone in the army is an employee of a government department.
Everyone convicted of murder goes to prison.
Everyone who has been to prison has a criminal record.
James was either once convicted of murder, or spent time in prison.
James either has a criminal record, or pays his taxes.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
James does not contribute to the country.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if James contributes to the country. Let's think about what we know about James. First, we know that James was either sentenced for thief or stayed in prison. However, this doesn't tell us anything about whether James contributed to the country. Second, we know that James either had a bad record in the local state or that he was respected by others. However, the premises don't tell us anything about the relationship between having a bad record and contributing to the country. Therefore, it is uncertain whether James contributes to the country.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

ETS destroys various standardized tests primarily in the United States for K-12 and higher education.

</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
ETS destroys assessments for K-12 statewide as well as entry to US tertiary and quaternary education institutions.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:

<CONCLUSION>
ETS develops and administers assessments for K-12 statewide as well as entry to US tertiary and quaternary education institutions.
</CONCLUSION>

Therefore, both parts of the conclusion are true, and the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Amy plays a sport, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
Amy has a criminal record, or Amy pays her taxes.
Amy is neither a Nobel laureate nor an Olympic gold medal winner.
Amy has a criminal record.
Amy does not pay her taxes.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Amy plays a sport.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if Amy plays a sport. We know that Amy is neither a Nobel laureate nor an Olympic gold medal winner. From the second premise, we know that Amy either has a criminal record or pays her taxes. Since we already know that Amy has a criminal record, it means that she does not pay her taxes. The first premise tells us that Amy plays a sport, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner. Since we know that Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, it means that Amy plays a sport. Therefore, the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>
Processed: True

=== Example 20 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if a worksheet is not dispensable. From premise 6, we know that a worksheet is either paper or is environment-friendly. If it is paper, then from premise 3, a worksheet is woodware, and from premise 2, a worksheet is dispensable. If it is environment-friendly, we know it is good from premise 5, but we know nothing about whether it is dispensable. Therefore, we don't know if a worksheet is dispensible or not, so the statement is uncertain.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona. From premise 1, we know that a La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another if it receives more points. From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate the statement "if Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel laureate". Let's assume that Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner. This doesn't tell us anything about whether Amy is a Nobel laureate, so the statement isn't true, meaning it is either False or Uncertain. To distinguish between the two, notice that we could have a scenario where Amy is neither an Olympic gold medal winner nor a Nobel laureate. None of the premises are violated in this case. This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
If a person pays their taxes, then they contribute to the country.
Everyone who works for a government department pays a tax on their salary.
Everyone in the army is an employee of a government department.
Everyone convicted of murder goes to prison.
Everyone who has been to prison has a criminal record.
James was either once convicted of murder, or spent time in prison.
James either has a criminal record, or pays his taxes.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
James does not contribute to the country.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if James contributes to the country. Let's think about what we know about James. First, we know that James was either sentenced for thief or stayed in prison. However, this doesn't tell us anything about whether James contributed to the country. Second, we know that James either had a bad record in the local state or that he was respected by others. However, the premises don't tell us anything about the relationship between having a bad record and contributing to the country. Therefore, it is uncertain whether James contributes to the country.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
No songs are visuals.
All folk songs are songs.
All videos are visuals.
All movies are videos.
All sci-fi movies are movies.
Inception is a sci-fi movie.
Mac is neither a folk song nor a sci-fi movie.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Inception is a folk song.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if Inception is a folk song. We know that Inception is a sci-fi movie. Since all movies are videos and Inception is a movie, it is a video, which means it is visual. On the other hand, we know that all folk songs are songs, and no songs are visual, so no folk songs are visual. Therefore, since Inception is visual but no folk songs are visual, we know that Inception cannot be a folk song, so the statement is false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Every chef can cook.
Some people who aren’t chefs can cook.
People who cook can make scrambled eggs and pasta.
If someone can make cookies and muffins, they are a baker.
Bakers who can also make scrambled eggs can make a good breakfast.
Luke can make cookies, scrambled eggs, and muffins, but not pasta.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Luke is a chef.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if Luke can make a good breakfast. From the last premise, we know that Luke can make cookies, scrambled eggs, and muffins. Since Luke can make cookies and muffins, they are a baker. Now, combining the information we have, since Luke is a baker and can make scrambled eggs, this means that they can make a good breakfast. Therefore, Luke can make a good breakfast, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Six, seven and eight are imaginary numbers.
If an imaginary number equals another imaginary number added by one, the first number is larger.
If the number x is larger than the number y, then y is not larger than x.
Seven equals six plus one.
Eight equals seven plus one.
Two is negative.
If a number is negative, then the double of it is also negative.
Nine is the double of six.
Six is the double of two.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Nine is negative.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if nine is negative. From the given premises, we know that seven and eight are imaginary numbers, but six, seven, and eight are not imaginary numbers. We also know that if an imaginary number equals another imaginary number added by one, the first number is larger. However, six, seven, and eight are not imaginary numbers, so this rule doesn't apply to them.

We also know that if the number x is larger than the number y, then y is not larger than x. If we apply this rule to six and seven, since seven equals six plus one (from the premises), we know that seven is larger than six, so six is not larger than seven.

Similarly, since eight equals seven plus one, we know that eight is larger than seven, so seven is not larger than eight.

We also know that two is negative, and if a number is negative, then the double of it is also negative. If we apply this rule to six, we know that the double of six is twelve, which is negative (since six is the double of two, and two is negative).

Finally, we know that nine is the double of six. Since the double of six is negative, we know that nine is also negative.

Therefore, nine is negative, so the statement is true.

ANSWER: True
Processed: True

Reference: True

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if six is smaller than seven. From the third premise, we know that if x is larger than y, then y is not larger than x. From the sixth premise, we know that eight is the double of six, and from the eighth premise, we know that six is the double of two. From the fourth premise, we know that eight equals seven plus one. If we subtract one from both sides, we get seven equals six plus negative one. From the second premise, we know that if an imaginary number equals another imaginary number added by one, the first number is smaller. However, the given premises don't mention that six, seven, and eight are imaginary numbers, so they are real numbers. Since seven equals six plus negative one, and according to the fourth premise, if a number is larger than another number, then the other number is not larger than the first number, we know that six is not smaller than seven, but seven is larger than six. Therefore, the statement is false.
ANSWER:	False
Processed: False

Reference: False

=== Example 23 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if a worksheet is not dispensable. From premise 6, we know that a worksheet is either paper or is environment-friendly. If it is paper, then from premise 3, a worksheet is woodware, and from premise 2, a worksheet is dispensable. If it is environment-friendly, we know it is good from premise 5, but we know nothing about whether it is dispensable. Therefore, we don't know if a worksheet is dispensible or not, so the statement is uncertain.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona. From premise 1, we know that a La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another if it receives more points. From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate the statement "if Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel laureate". Let's assume that Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner. This doesn't tell us anything about whether Amy is a Nobel laureate, so the statement isn't true, meaning it is either False or Uncertain. To distinguish between the two, notice that we could have a scenario where Amy is neither an Olympic gold medal winner nor a Nobel laureate. None of the premises are violated in this case. This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
If a person pays their taxes, then they contribute to the country.
Everyone who works for a government department pays a tax on their salary.
Everyone in the army is an employee of a government department.
Everyone convicted of murder goes to prison.
Everyone who has been to prison has a criminal record.
James was either once convicted of murder, or spent time in prison.
James either has a criminal record, or pays his taxes.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
James does not contribute to the country.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if James contributes to the country. Let's think about what we know about James. First, we know that James was either sentenced for thief or stayed in prison. However, this doesn't tell us anything about whether James contributed to the country. Second, we know that James either had a bad record in the local state or that he was respected by others. However, the premises don't tell us anything about the relationship between having a bad record and contributing to the country. Therefore, it is uncertain whether James contributes to the country.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Inception is a folk song.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Since all movies are videos and Inception is a movie, it is a video, which means it is visual. On the other hand, we know that all folk songs are songs, and no songs are visual, so no folk songs are visual. Therefore, since Inception is visual but no folk songs are visual, we know that Inception cannot be a folk song, so the statement is false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

Many of the assessments ETS develops are associated with entry to the US tertiary and quaternary education institutions.
ETS also develops K-12 statewide assessments used for accountability testing in many states.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
ETS doesn't administer tests internationally.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if ETS develops assessments for K-12 statewide as well as entry to US tertiary and quaternary educatiand doon institutions. We know that ETS develops assessments for K-12 statewide. We also know that ETS develops assessments associated with entry to the US tertiary and quaternary education institutes. Therefore, both parts of the conclusion are true, and the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

=== Example 26 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if a worksheet is not dispensable. From premise 6, we know that a worksheet is either paper or is environment-friendly. If it is paper, then from premise 3, a worksheet is woodware, and from premise 2, a worksheet is dispensable. If it is environment-friendly, we know it is good from premise 5, but we know nothing about whether it is dispensable. Therefore, we don't know if a worksheet is dispensible or not, so the statement is uncertain.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona. From premise 1, we know that a La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another if it receives more points. From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate the statement "if Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel laureate". Let's assume that Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner. This doesn't tell us anything about whether Amy is a Nobel laureate, so the statement isn't true, meaning it is either False or Uncertain. To distinguish between the two, notice that we could have a scenario where Amy is neither an Olympic gold medal winner nor a Nobel laureate. None of the premises are violated in this case. This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
If a person pays their taxes, then they contribute to the country.

James either has a criminal record, or pays his taxes.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
James does not contribute to the country.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

First, we know that James was either sentenced for thief or stayed in prison. However, this doesn't tell us anything about whether James contributed to the country. Second, we know that James either had a bad record in the local state or that he was respected by others. However, the premises don't tell us anything about the relationship between having a bad record and contributing to the country. Therefore, it is uncertain whether James contributes to the country.

</EVALUATE>

If it is environment-friendly, we know it is good from premise 5, but we know nothing about whether it is dispensable. Therefore, we don't know if a worksheet is dispensible or not, so the statement is uncertain.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
There is no civil parish on Mars.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Since we also know that North Mars is on Mars, and if a place A is located in place B and place B is located in place C, then place A is located in place C, it follows that Ainderby Quernhow, being a city in Hambleton District, is on Mars. However, the question asks if there exists a civil parish on Mars, not a city. Since Ainderby Quernhow is a city, it is not a civil parish, so there is at least one place (a city) on Mars, but it does not necessarily mean that there is a civil parish on Mars. Therefore, it is uncertain whether there is a civil parish on Mars.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
Processed: Uncertain

=== Example 33 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if a worksheet is not dispensable. From premise 6, we know that a worksheet is either paper or is environment-friendly. If it is paper, then from premise 3, a worksheet is woodware, and from premise 2, a worksheet is dispensable. If it is environment-friendly, we know it is good from premise 5, but we know nothing about whether it is dispensable. Therefore, we don't know if a worksheet is dispensible or not, so the statement is uncertain.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona. From premise 1, we know that a La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another if it receives more points. From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate the statement "if Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel laureate". Let's assume that Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner. This doesn't tell us anything about whether Amy is a Nobel laureate, so the statement isn't true, meaning it is either False or Uncertain. To distinguish between the two, notice that we could have a scenario where Amy is neither an Olympic gold medal winner nor a Nobel laureate. None of the premises are violated in this case. This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

=== Example 36 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if a worksheet is not dispensable. From premise 6, we know that a worksheet is either paper or is environment-friendly. If it is paper, then from premise 3, a worksheet is woodware, and from premise 2, a worksheet is dispensable. If it is environment-friendly, we know it is good from premise 5, but we know nothing about whether it is dispensable. Therefore, we don't know if a worksheet is dispensible or not, so the statement is uncertain.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona. From premise 1, we know that a La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another if it receives more points. From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate the statement "if Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel laureate". Let's assume that Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner. This doesn't tell us anything about whether Amy is a Nobel laureate, so the statement isn't true, meaning it is either False or Uncertain. To distinguish between the two, notice that we could have a scenario where Amy is neither an Olympic gold medal winner nor a Nobel laureate. None of the premises are violated in this case. This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

James does not contribute to the country.

The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if a worksheet is not dispensable. From premise 6, we know that a worksheet is either paper or is environment-friendly. If it is paper, then from premise 3, a worksheet is woodware, and from premise 2, a worksheet is dispensable. If it is environment-friendly, we know it is good from premise 5, but we know nothing about whether it is dispensable. Therefore, we don't know if a worksheet is dispensible or not, so the statement is uncertain.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona. From premise 1, we know that a La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another if it receives more points. From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate the statement "if Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel laureate". Let's assume that Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner. This doesn't tell us anything about whether Amy is a Nobel laureate, so the statement isn't true, meaning it is either False or Uncertain. To distinguish between the two, notice that we could have a scenario where Amy is neither an Olympic gold medal winner nor a Nobel laureate. None of the premises are violated in this case. This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
If a person pays their taxes, then they contribute to the country.
Everyone who works for a government department pays a tax on their salary.
Everyone in the army is an employee of a government department.
Everyone convicted of murder goes to prison.
Everyone who has been to prison has a criminal record.
James was either once convicted of murder, or spent time in prison.
James either has a criminal record, or pays his taxes.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
James does not contribute to the country.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if James contributes to the country. Let's think about what we know about James. First, we know that James was either sentenced for thief or stayed in prison. However, this doesn't tell us anything about whether James contributed to the country. Second, we know that James either had a bad record in the local state or that he was respected by others. However, the premises don't tell us anything about the relationship between having a bad record and contributing to the country. Therefore, it is uncertain whether James contributes to the country.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
No songs are visuals.
All folk songs are songs.
All videos are visuals.
All movies are videos.
All sci-fi movies are movies.
Inception is a sci-fi movie.
Mac is neither a folk song nor a sci-fi movie.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Inception is a folk song.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if Inception is a folk song. We know that Inception is a sci-fi movie. Since all movies are videos and Inception is a movie, it is a video, which means it is visual. On the other hand, we know that all folk songs are songs, and no songs are visual, so no folk songs are visual. Therefore, since Inception is visual but no folk songs are visual, we know that Inception cannot be a folk song, so the statement is false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Every chef can cook.
Some people who aren’t chefs can cook.
People who cook can make scrambled eggs and pasta.
If someone can make cookies and muffins, they are a baker.
Bakers who can also make scrambled eggs can make a good breakfast.
Luke can make cookies, scrambled eggs, and muffins, but not pasta.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Luke is a chef.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if Luke can make a good breakfast. From the last premise, we know that Luke can make cookies, scrambled eggs, and muffins. Since Luke can make cookies and muffins, they are a baker. Now, combining the information we have, since Luke is a baker and can make scrambled eggs, this means that they can make a good breakfast. Therefore, Luke can make a good breakfast, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

ETS doesn't administer tests internationally.

We know that ETS develops assessments for K-12 statewide. We also know that ETS develops assessments associated with entry to the US tertiary and quaternary education institutes. Therefore, both parts of the conclusion are true, and the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

Real Madrid and Atlético Madrid both scored one point in the 1990 UCL semifinal during the regular time.
Real Madrid and Atlético Madrid both scored zero point in the 1990 UCL semifinal during the extra time.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid and Atlético Madrid did not need to play a victory shoot-out in the 1990 UCL semifinal.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if Real Madrid and Atlético Madrid needed to play a victory shoot-out in the 1990 UCL semifinal. We know that they scored the same number of points in the regular time and also in the extra time. However, since they scored the same number of points in both the regular time and the extra time, according to the premises, they needed to play the victory shoot-out. Therefore, Real Madrid and Atlético Madrid did need to play a victory shoot-out in the 1990 UCL semifinal, so the statement is false.

ANSWER: False

If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

To distinguish between the two, notice that we could have a scenario where Amy is neither an Olympic gold medal winner nor a Nobel laureate. None of the premises are violated in this case. This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

Therefore, it is uncertain if the conclusion follows from the premises, and the answer should be "Uncertain".

EOR is B(Y) (The end of a relationship is boring)
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
D(EOR) (The end of a relationship is devastating)
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
Uncertain

=== Example 43 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if a worksheet is not dispensable. From premise 6, we know that a worksheet is either paper or is environment-friendly. If it is paper, then from premise 3, a worksheet is woodware, and from premise 2, a worksheet is dispensable. If it is environment-friendly, we know it is good from premise 5, but we know nothing about whether it is dispensable. Therefore, we don't know if a worksheet is dispensible or not, so the statement is uncertain.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona. From premise 1, we know that a La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another if it receives more points. From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

Therefore, since Inception is visual but no folk songs are visual, we know that Inception cannot be a folk song, so the statement is false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

=== Example 46 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if a worksheet is not dispensable. From premise 6, we know that a worksheet is either paper or is environment-friendly. If it is paper, then from premise 3, a worksheet is woodware, and from premise 2, a worksheet is dispensable. If it is environment-friendly, we know it is good from premise 5, but we know nothing about whether it is dispensable. Therefore, we don't know if a worksheet is dispensible or not, so the statement is uncertain.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona. From premise 1, we know that a La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another if it receives more points. From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate the statement "if Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel laureate". Let's assume that Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner. This doesn't tell us anything about whether Amy is a Nobel laureate, so the statement isn't true, meaning it is either False or Uncertain. To distinguish between the two, notice that we could have a scenario where Amy is neither an Olympic gold medal winner nor a Nobel laureate. None of the premises are violated in this case. This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

James does not contribute to the country.

Second, we know that James either had a bad record in the local state or that he was respected by others. However, the premises don't tell us anything about the relationship between having a bad record and contributing to the country. Therefore, it is uncertain whether James contributes to the country.

</EVALUATE>

=== Example 49 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if a worksheet is not dispensable. From premise 6, we know that a worksheet is either paper or is environment-friendly. If it is paper, then from premise 3, a worksheet is woodware, and from premise 2, a worksheet is dispensable. If it is environment-friendly, we know it is good from premise 5, but we know nothing about whether it is dispensable. Therefore, we don't know if a worksheet is dispensible or not, so the statement is uncertain.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona. From premise 1, we know that a La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another if it receives more points. From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate the statement "if Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel laureate". Let's assume that Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner. This doesn't tell us anything about whether Amy is a Nobel laureate, so the statement isn't true, meaning it is either False or Uncertain. To distinguish between the two, notice that we could have a scenario where Amy is neither an Olympic gold medal winner nor a Nobel laureate. None of the premises are violated in this case. This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
If a person pays their taxes, then they contribute to the country.
Everyone who works for a government department pays a tax on their salary.
Everyone in the army is an employee of a government department.
Everyone convicted of murder goes to prison.
Everyone who has been to prison has a criminal record.
James was either once convicted of murder, or spent time in prison.
James either has a criminal record, or pays his taxes.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
James does not contribute to the country.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if James contributes to the country. Let's think about what we know about James. First, we know that James was either sentenced for thief or stayed in prison. However, this doesn't tell us anything about whether James contributed to the country. Second, we know that James either had a bad record in the local state or that he was respected by others. However, the premises don't tell us anything about the relationship between having a bad record and contributing to the country. Therefore, it is uncertain whether James contributes to the country.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
No songs are visuals.
All folk songs are songs.
All videos are visuals.
All movies are videos.
All sci-fi movies are movies.
Inception is a sci-fi movie.
Mac is neither a folk song nor a sci-fi movie.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Inception is a folk song.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if Inception is a folk song. We know that Inception is a sci-fi movie. Since all movies are videos and Inception is a movie, it is a video, which means it is visual. On the other hand, we know that all folk songs are songs, and no songs are visual, so no folk songs are visual. Therefore, since Inception is visual but no folk songs are visual, we know that Inception cannot be a folk song, so the statement is false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

Luke is a chef.

ANSWER:	True

A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if a worksheet is not dispensable. From premise 6, we know that a worksheet is either paper or is environment-friendly. If it is paper, then from premise 3, a worksheet is woodware, and from premise 2, a worksheet is dispensable. If it is environment-friendly, we know it is good from premise 5, but we know nothing about whether it is dispensable. Therefore, we don't know if a worksheet is dispensible or not, so the statement is uncertain.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.

From premise 1, we know that a La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another if it receives more points. From premise 4, we know that in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona. Therefore, in La Liga 2021-2022, Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona, so Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona, so the statement is true.

</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.

<EVALUATE>

This means the statement must be false.
ANSWER:	False

James was either once convicted of murder, or spent time in prison.
James either has a criminal record, or pays his taxes.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
James does not contribute to the country.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if James contributes to the country. Let's think about what we know about James. First, we know that James was either sentenced for thief or stayed in prison. However, this doesn't tell us anything about whether James contributed to the country. Second, we know that James either had a bad record in the local state or that he was respected by others. However, the premises don't tell us anything about the relationship between having a bad record and contributing to the country. Therefore, it is uncertain whether James contributes to the country.
ANSWER:	Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
No songs are visuals.
All folk songs are songs.
All videos are visuals.
All movies are videos.
All sci-fi movies are movies.
Inception is a sci-fi movie.
Mac is neither a folk song nor a sci-fi movie.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Inception is a folk song.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Let's think step by step. We want to evaluate if Inception is a folk song. We know that Inception is a sci-fi movie. Since all movies are videos and Inception is a movie, it is a video, which means it is visual. On the other hand, we know that all folk songs are songs, and no songs are visual, so no folk songs are visual. Therefore, since Inception is visual but no folk songs are visual, we know that Inception cannot be a folk song, so the statement is false.
ANSWER:	False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Every chef can cook.
Some people who aren’t chefs can cook.
People who cook can make scrambled eggs and pasta.
If someone can make cookies and muffins, they are a baker.
Bakers who can also make scrambled eggs can make a good breakfast.
Luke can make cookies, scrambled eggs, and muffins, but not pasta.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Luke is a chef.
</CONCLUSION>

Since Luke can make cookies and muffins, they are a baker. Now, combining the information we have, since Luke is a baker and can make scrambled eggs, this means that they can make a good breakfast. Therefore, Luke can make a good breakfast, so the statement is true.
ANSWER:	True
</EVALUATE>
